## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features x (position), v (velocity), and t (time) are the standard state variables for second-order mechanical oscillators. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators typically express dv_dt as a sum of restoring-force terms (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v and possibly x), and optional time-dependent forcing or parametric modulation (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal spring-mass, small oscillations)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in linear regime)
- Constant bias/tilt force: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (gravity offset, DC actuation, equilibrium shift)
- Cubic stiffness (Duffing, hardening/softening): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 (nonlinear spring restoring force)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 - c3 * x**5 (stronger nonlinearity at larger amplitudes)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping, amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Nonlinear damping coupled to displacement: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (material/geometry-induced amplitude-dependent damping)
- Van der Pol-type self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle formation)
- Liénard form (general nonlinear oscillator): dv_dt = -g0 * x - g1 * x**3 - (f0 + f1 * x**2) * v (broad class including Duffing/van der Pol variants)
- Periodic external forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven oscillator, resonance/entrainment)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type behavior, parametric resonance)
- Non-smooth/impact-like restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x * Abs(x) (piecewise-stiffness or contact-like nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dv_dt depends mainly on x (and not v), the system is approximately conservative; dv_dt often matches the negative gradient of an effective potential, favoring odd-in-x restoring terms (x, x**3, x**5).
- Terms linear in v indicate viscous dissipation; deviations such as v*Abs(v) or x**2*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping that changes decay rate with oscillation size.
- Odd polynomial restoring forces (x + x**3 + x**5) typically preserve left-right symmetry in x; even-in-x restoring components imply asymmetric potentials or biased loading.
- A factor like (c0 - x**2) * v signals state-dependent damping that can become negative and create self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles).
- Explicit t-dependence (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) usually indicates external drive; the drive frequency parameter inside sin/cos controls resonance structure.
- Time-dependent multiplication of x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicates parametric modulation of stiffness and suggests Mathieu/parametric-instability regions.
- Cross terms that multiply x and v (or x**2 and v) often represent geometric nonlinearities or velocity-dependent forces that strengthen with displacement amplitude.
- Non-smooth structures using Abs(x) (e.g., x*Abs(x)) can approximate piecewise stiffness/contact effects and typically produce sharper waveform corners or amplitude-dependent frequency shifts.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO11)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidate formulas: 66

GT (fixed):  
\[
-2.5126990598325\,x^3\;-\;2.5126990598325\,x(0.0921849151045819\,t+1)\;-\;0.774919680656294\,\sin(v)
\]
So GT is exactly a sum of three parts: (i) \(x^3\) term, (ii) \(x\) and \(t x\) terms, (iii) a pure \(\sin(v)\) term. No constants, no other \(t\)-only terms, no \(v\)-polynomials, no absolute values, no denominators, etc.

Key requirement for any candidate: it must be able to reduce to
\[
A x^3 + B x + C t x + D\sin(v)
\]
with the specific numeric coefficients above, and **no extra leftover terms**.

Also, candidates using \(\cos(\alpha v+\phi)\) can match \(\sin(v)\) by phase shift: \(\cos(v+\pi/2)=-\sin(v)\), etc. But they must also allow \(\alpha=1\) (or \(\alpha=-1\)) and an appropriate phase.

---

### 1. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(c4 v+c5) + c6 \frac{x^{c7}}{c8+x^{c7}}\)
The rational term cannot be made identically 0 for all \(x\) except by setting \(c6=0\). Then we have linear + cubic + \(tx\) + cosine, which can phase-shift to sine. **Match possible**.

### 2. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5\cos(c6 v+c7)\)
The \(e^{c4 t}\) term must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Remaining terms can match (cos→sin via phase). **Match possible**.

### 3. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 e^{c7 t}\cos(\cdot)\)
Need to remove the extra \(e^{c7 t}\cos(\cdot)\): set \(c6=0\). Then same as #1 without rational. **Match possible**.

### 4. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3 t^{c4} + c5\cos(\cdot)\)
Must remove \(t^{c4}\): set \(c3=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 5. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2\sin(c3 t+c4) + c5 t x + c6\cos(\cdot)\)
Must remove \(\sin(\text{in }t)\): set \(c2=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 6. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 \frac{t}{c7 v+c8} + c9\frac{1}{c7 v+c8}\)
The \(1/(c7 v+c8)\) terms are not in GT; must set \(c6=c9=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 7. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6\sin(c7 x+c8)\cos(c9 t)\)
Extra oscillatory-in-\(x,t\) term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 8. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 \frac{t}{c7 x+c8} + c9\frac{1}{c7 x+c8}\)
Denominator-in-\(x\) terms must vanish: set \(c6=c9=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 9. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 \frac{t}{c7 t+c8} + c9\frac{1}{c7 t+c8}\)
These are non-polynomial in \(t\); must set \(c6=c9=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 10. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 t + c7\)
GT has no pure \(t\) or constant term; must set \(c6=0, c7=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 11. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 t (c7+v)^{c8}\)
Extra \(t\cdot f(v)\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 12. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 t (c7+x)^{c8}\)
Extra \(t\cdot f(x)\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 13. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6\log(c7 t+1)\)
Log term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 14. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 \frac{v}{c7 t+c8} + c9\frac{1}{c7 t+c8}\)
Non-GT rational terms; set \(c6=c9=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 15. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 \frac{x}{c7 t+c8} + c9\frac{1}{c7 t+c8}\)
Those are not polynomial in \(t\); must set \(c6=c9=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 16. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 x^{c7}\sin(c8 t+c9)\)
Extra \(x^{c7}\sin(t)\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 17. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2\sin(c3 v+c4) + c5 x^3 + c6 v^{c7} + c8 t x + c9 v|v|\)
GT has no \(v\), \(v^{c7}\), or \(v|v|\) terms. You can set \(c1=0,c6=0,c9=0\). Then you have \(x, x^3, tx,\sin(\text{affine }v)\) which can match \(\sin(v)\) by setting \(c3=\pm1\) and phase. **Match possible**.

### 18. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3 v^{c4} + c5\cos(\cdot)\)
Must remove \(v^{c4}\): set \(c3=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 19. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 x^{c7} e^{c8|v|}\)
The \(e^{c8|v|}\) dependence cannot be turned into a pure \(\sin(v)\); must remove it: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 20. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3 x^{c4} + c5\cos(\cdot)\)
Extra \(x^{c4}\) must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 21. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 x^3 + c3 v^3 + c4 t x + c5 v|v| + c6\cos(c7 v + c8 e^{c9 x^2})\)
The cosine argument depends on \(x\) unless \(c8=0\) (or \(c9=0\) still leaves \(e^{0}=1\) giving a constant shift; that’s okay too). But GT needs \(\sin(v)\) with no \(x\) in the phase, so set \(c8=0\). Also remove \(v, v^3, v|v|\): set \(c1=c3=c5=0\). Then we have \(x,x^3,tx,\cos(c7 v)\) which can phase to \(\sin(v)\) by choosing \(c7=\pm1\) and phase via adding a constant—however with \(c8=0\) the phase constant is 0; but we can still get \(\sin\) only if we can shift phase. Here cosine is \(\cos(c7 v + 0)\) only; no free phase unless \(c8 e^{c9 x^2}\) provided it, but we set \(c8=0\). So we cannot create \(\cos(v+\phi)\) with \(\phi\neq 0\). Therefore cannot match \(-0.7749\sin(v)\) exactly (since \(\cos(v)\neq \sin(v)\) globally). **No match**.

### 22. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2\sin(c3 v+c4) + c5 t x + c6\cos(c7 v+c8)\)
GT needs only one sinusoid in \(v\). We can set one trig coefficient to 0, e.g. \(c6=0\), and tune \(\sin(c3 v+c4)\) to \(\sin(v)\). Then linear+cubic+tx present. **Match possible**.

### 23. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 t x + c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 v (c7+t)^{c8}\)
Extra \(v\cdot f(t)\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then linear+cubic+tx+cos. **Match possible**.

### 24. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 v + c3 v x^2 + c4 t x + c5\cos(\cdot)\)

### 25. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2\sin(\cdot) + c5 x^3 + c6 v^3 + c7 t x + c8 x\cos(c9 t)\)
